    45	CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE
    46	_timescaledb_functions.policy_compression_execute(
    47	  job_id              INTEGER,
    48	  htid                INTEGER,
    49	  lag                 ANYELEMENT,
    50	  maxchunks           INTEGER,
    51	  verbose_log         BOOLEAN,
    52	  recompress_enabled  BOOLEAN,
    53	  reindex_enabled     BOOLEAN,
    54	  use_creation_time   BOOLEAN
    55	)
    56	AS $$
    57	DECLARE
    58	  htoid       REGCLASS;
    59	  chunk_rec   RECORD;
    60	  idx_rec     RECORD;
    61	  numchunks_compressed   INTEGER := 0;
    62	  _message     text;
    63	  _detail      text;
    64	  _sqlstate    text;
    65	  -- fully compressed chunk status
    66	  status_fully_compressed int := 1;
    67	  -- chunk status bits:
    68	  bit_compressed int := 1;
    69	  bit_compressed_unordered int := 2;
    70	  bit_frozen int := 4;
    71	  bit_compressed_partial int := 8;
    72	  creation_lag INTERVAL := NULL;
    73	  chunks_failure INTEGER := 0;
    74	BEGIN
    75	
    76	  -- procedures with SET clause cannot execute transaction
    77	  -- control so we adjust search_path in procedure body
    78	  SET LOCAL search_path TO pg_catalog, pg_temp;
    79	
    80	  SELECT format('%I.%I', schema_name, table_name) INTO htoid
    81	  FROM _timescaledb_catalog.hypertable
    82	  WHERE id = htid;
    83	
    84	  -- for the integer cases, we have to compute the lag w.r.t
    85	  -- the integer_now function and then pass on to show_chunks
    86	  IF pg_typeof(lag) IN ('BIGINT'::regtype, 'INTEGER'::regtype, 'SMALLINT'::regtype) THEN
    87	    -- cannot have use_creation_time set with this
    88	    IF use_creation_time IS TRUE THEN
    89	        RAISE EXCEPTION 'job % cannot use creation time with integer_now function', job_id;
    90	    END IF;
    91	    lag := _timescaledb_functions.subtract_integer_from_now(htoid, lag::BIGINT);
    92	  END IF;
    93	
    94	  -- if use_creation_time has been specified then the lag needs to be used with the
    95	  -- "compress_created_before" argument. Otherwise the usual "older_than" argument
    96	  -- is good enough
    97	  IF use_creation_time IS TRUE THEN
    98	    creation_lag := lag;
    99	    lag := NULL;
   100	  END IF;
   101	
   102	  FOR chunk_rec IN
   103	    SELECT
   104	      show.oid, ch.schema_name, ch.table_name, ch.status
   105	    FROM
   106	      @extschema@.show_chunks(htoid, older_than => lag, created_before => creation_lag) AS show(oid)
   107	      INNER JOIN pg_class pgc ON pgc.oid = show.oid
   108	      INNER JOIN pg_namespace pgns ON pgc.relnamespace = pgns.oid
   109	      INNER JOIN _timescaledb_catalog.chunk ch ON ch.table_name = pgc.relname AND ch.schema_name = pgns.nspname AND ch.hypertable_id = htid
   110	    WHERE NOT ch.dropped
   111	    AND NOT ch.osm_chunk
   112	    -- Checking for chunks which are not fully compressed and not frozen
   113	    AND ch.status != status_fully_compressed
   114	    AND ch.status & bit_frozen = 0
   115	  LOOP
   116	    BEGIN
   117	      IF chunk_rec.status = bit_compressed OR recompress_enabled IS TRUE THEN
   118	        PERFORM @extschema@.compress_chunk(chunk_rec.oid);
   119	        numchunks_compressed := numchunks_compressed + 1;
   120	      END IF;
   121	    EXCEPTION WHEN OTHERS THEN
   122	      GET STACKED DIAGNOSTICS
   123	          _message = MESSAGE_TEXT,
   124	          _detail = PG_EXCEPTION_DETAIL,
   125	          _sqlstate = RETURNED_SQLSTATE;
   126	      RAISE WARNING 'converting chunk "%" to columnstore failed when recompress columnstore policy is executed', chunk_rec.oid::regclass::text
   127	          USING DETAIL = format('Message: (%s), Detail: (%s).', _message, _detail),
   128	                ERRCODE = _sqlstate;
   129	      chunks_failure := chunks_failure + 1;
   130	    END;
   131	    COMMIT;
   132	
   133	    -- went through recompression successfully now reindex indexes
   134	    IF (chunk_rec.status & bit_compressed_partial = bit_compressed_partial) AND (reindex_enabled IS TRUE) THEN
   135	      FOR idx_rec IN
   136	        SELECT idx.schemaname, idx.indexname
   137	        FROM pg_indexes idx
   138	        JOIN _timescaledb_catalog.chunk ch ON ch.schema_name = idx.schemaname AND ch.table_name = idx.tablename
   139	        WHERE idx.schemaname = chunk_rec.schema_name
   140	          AND idx.tablename = chunk_rec.table_name
   141	          AND ch.status = status_fully_compressed
   142	      LOOP
   143	        BEGIN
   144	          EXECUTE format('REINDEX INDEX %I.%I;', idx_rec.schemaname, idx_rec.indexname);
   145	        EXCEPTION WHEN OTHERS THEN
   146	          GET STACKED DIAGNOSTICS
   147	              _message = MESSAGE_TEXT,
   148	              _detail = PG_EXCEPTION_DETAIL,
   149	              _sqlstate = RETURNED_SQLSTATE;
   150	          RAISE WARNING 'reindexing index "%.%" for chunk "%" to columnstore failed when columnstore policy is executed', idx_rec.schemaname, idx_rec.indexname, chunk_rec.oid::regclass::text
   151	              USING DETAIL = format('Message: (%s), Detail: (%s).', _message, _detail),
   152	                    ERRCODE = _sqlstate;
   153	          chunks_failure := chunks_failure + 1;
   154	        END;
   155	        COMMIT;
   156	      END LOOP;
   157	    END IF;
   158	
   159	    -- SET LOCAL is only active until end of transaction.
   160	    -- While we could use SET at the start of the function we do not
   161	    -- want to bleed out search_path to caller, so we do SET LOCAL
   162	    -- again after COMMIT
   163	    SET LOCAL search_path TO pg_catalog, pg_temp;
   164	    IF verbose_log THEN
   165	       RAISE LOG 'job % completed processing chunk %.%', job_id, chunk_rec.schema_name, chunk_rec.table_name;
   166	    END IF;
   167	    IF maxchunks > 0 AND numchunks_compressed >= maxchunks THEN
   168	         EXIT;
   169	    END IF;
   170	  END LOOP;
   171	
   172	  IF chunks_failure > 0 THEN
   173	    RAISE EXCEPTION 'columnstore policy failure'
   174	      USING
   175	        DETAIL = format('Failed to convert %L chunks to columnstore. Successfully converted %L chunks.', chunks_failure, numchunks_compressed),
   176	        ERRCODE = 'data_exception';
   177	  END IF;
   178	END;
   179	$$ LANGUAGE PLPGSQL;
   180	
   181	CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE
   182	_timescaledb_functions.policy_compression(job_id INTEGER, config JSONB)
   183	AS $$
   184	DECLARE
   185	  dimtype             REGTYPE;
   186	  dimtypeinput        REGPROC;
   187	  compress_after      TEXT;
   188	  compress_created_before TEXT;
   189	  lag_value           TEXT;
   190	  lag_bigint_value    BIGINT;
   191	  htid                INTEGER;
   192	  htoid               REGCLASS;
   193	  chunk_rec           RECORD;
   194	  verbose_log         BOOL;
   195	  maxchunks           INTEGER := 0;
   196	  numchunks           INTEGER := 1;
   197	  recompress_enabled  BOOL;
   198	  reindex_enabled     BOOL;
   199	  use_creation_time   BOOL := FALSE;
   200	BEGIN
   201	
   202	  -- procedures with SET clause cannot execute transaction
   203	  -- control so we adjust search_path in procedure body
   204	  SET LOCAL search_path TO pg_catalog, pg_temp;
   205	
   206	  IF config IS NULL THEN
   207	    RAISE EXCEPTION 'job % has null config', job_id;
   208	  END IF;
   209	
   210	  htid := jsonb_object_field_text(config, 'hypertable_id')::INTEGER;
   211	  IF htid is NULL THEN
   212	    RAISE EXCEPTION 'job % config must have hypertable_id', job_id;
   213	  END IF;
   214	
   215	  verbose_log         := COALESCE(jsonb_object_field_text(config, 'verbose_log')::BOOLEAN, FALSE);
   216	  maxchunks           := COALESCE(jsonb_object_field_text(config, 'maxchunks_to_compress')::INTEGER, 0);
   217	  recompress_enabled  := COALESCE(jsonb_object_field_text(config, 'recompress')::BOOLEAN, TRUE);
   218	  reindex_enabled     := COALESCE(jsonb_object_field_text(config, 'reindex')::BOOLEAN, TRUE);
   219	
   220	  -- find primary dimension type --
   221	  SELECT dim.column_type INTO dimtype
   222	  FROM  _timescaledb_catalog.hypertable ht
   223	        JOIN _timescaledb_catalog.dimension dim ON ht.id = dim.hypertable_id
   224	  WHERE ht.id = htid
   225	  ORDER BY dim.id
   226	  LIMIT 1;
   227	
   228	  compress_after      := jsonb_object_field_text(config, 'compress_after');
   229	  IF compress_after IS NULL THEN
   230	    compress_created_before := jsonb_object_field_text(config, 'compress_created_before');
   231	    IF compress_created_before IS NULL THEN
   232	        RAISE EXCEPTION 'job % config must have compress_after or compress_created_before', job_id;
   233	    END IF;
   234	    lag_value := compress_created_before;
   235	    use_creation_time := true;
   236	    dimtype := 'INTERVAL' ::regtype;
   237	  ELSE
   238	    lag_value := compress_after;
   239	  END IF;
   240	
   241	  -- execute the properly type casts for the lag value
   242	  CASE dimtype
   243	    WHEN 'TIMESTAMP'::regtype, 'TIMESTAMPTZ'::regtype, 'DATE'::regtype, 'INTERVAL' ::regtype  THEN
   244	      CALL _timescaledb_functions.policy_compression_execute(job_id, htid, lag_value::INTERVAL, maxchunks, verbose_log, recompress_enabled, reindex_enabled, use_creation_time);
   245	    WHEN 'BIGINT'::regtype THEN
   246	      CALL _timescaledb_functions.policy_compression_execute(job_id, htid, lag_value::BIGINT, maxchunks, verbose_log, recompress_enabled, reindex_enabled, use_creation_time);
   247	    WHEN 'INTEGER'::regtype THEN
   248	      CALL _timescaledb_functions.policy_compression_execute(job_id, htid, lag_value::INTEGER, maxchunks, verbose_log, recompress_enabled, reindex_enabled, use_creation_time);
   249	    WHEN 'SMALLINT'::regtype THEN
   250	      CALL _timescaledb_functions.policy_compression_execute(job_id, htid, lag_value::SMALLINT, maxchunks, verbose_log, recompress_enabled, reindex_enabled, use_creation_time);
   251	  END CASE;
   252	  COMMIT;
   253	END;
   254	$$ LANGUAGE PLPGSQL;
   255

static void
json_add_dim_interval_value(JsonbParseState *parse_state, const char *json_label, Oid dim_type,
							Datum value)
{
	switch (dim_type)
	{
		case INTERVALOID:
			ts_jsonb_add_interval(parse_state, json_label, DatumGetIntervalP(value));
			break;
		case INT2OID:
			ts_jsonb_add_int64(parse_state, json_label, DatumGetInt16(value));
			break;
		case INT4OID:
			ts_jsonb_add_int64(parse_state, json_label, DatumGetInt32(value));
			break;
		case INT8OID:
			ts_jsonb_add_int64(parse_state, json_label, DatumGetInt64(value));
			break;
		default:
			ereport(ERROR,
					(errcode(ERRCODE_FEATURE_NOT_SUPPORTED),
					 errmsg("unsupported interval argument type, expected type : %s",
							format_type_be(dim_type))));
	}
}

static void
json_add_dim_interval_value(JsonbParseState *parse_state, const char *json_label, Oid dim_type,
							Datum value)
{
	switch (dim_type)
	{
		case INTERVALOID:
			ts_jsonb_add_interval(parse_state, json_label, DatumGetIntervalP(value));
			break;
		case INT2OID:
			ts_jsonb_add_int64(parse_state, json_label, DatumGetInt16(value));
			break;
		case INT4OID:
			ts_jsonb_add_int64(parse_state, json_label, DatumGetInt32(value));
			break;
		case INT8OID:
			ts_jsonb_add_int64(parse_state, json_label, DatumGetInt64(value));
			break;
		default:
			ereport(ERROR,
					(errcode(ERRCODE_FEATURE_NOT_SUPPORTED),
					 errmsg("unsupported interval argument type, expected type : %s",
							format_type_be(dim_type))));
	}
}

static Datum
convert_interval_arg(Oid dim_type, Datum interval, Oid *interval_type, const char *str_msg)
{
	Oid convert_to = dim_type;
	Datum converted;

	if (IS_TIMESTAMP_TYPE(dim_type))
		convert_to = INTERVALOID;

	if (*interval_type != convert_to)
	{
		if (!can_coerce_type(1, interval_type, &convert_to, COERCION_IMPLICIT))
		{
			if (IS_INTEGER_TYPE(dim_type))
				ereport(ERROR,
						(errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
						 errmsg("invalid parameter value for %s", str_msg),
						 errhint("Use time interval of type %s with the continuous aggregate.",
								 format_type_be(dim_type))));
			else if (IS_TIMESTAMP_TYPE(dim_type))
				ereport(ERROR,
						(errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
						 errmsg("invalid parameter value for %s", str_msg),
						 errhint("Use time interval with a continuous aggregate using "
								 "timestamp-based time "
								 "bucket.")));
		}
	}

	converted = ts_time_datum_convert_arg(interval, interval_type, convert_to);

	/* For integer types, first convert all types to int64 to get on a common
	 * type. Then check valid time ranges against the partition/dimension
	 * type */
	switch (*interval_type)
	{
		case INT2OID:
			converted = Int64GetDatum((int64) DatumGetInt16(converted));
			break;
		case INT4OID:
			converted = Int64GetDatum((int64) DatumGetInt32(converted));
			break;
		case INT8OID:
			break;
		case INTERVALOID:
			/* For timestamp types, we only support Interval, so nothing further
			 * to do. */
			return converted;
		default:
			pg_unreachable();
			break;
	}

	/* Cap at min and max */
	if (DatumGetInt64(converted) < ts_time_get_min(dim_type))
		converted = ts_time_get_min(dim_type);

   408	
   409	/*
   410	 * Enforce that a policy has a refresh window of at least two buckets to
   411	 * ensure we materialize at least one bucket each run.
   412	 *
   413	 * Why two buckets? Note that the policy probably won't execute at at time
   414	 * that exactly aligns with a bucket boundary, so a window of one bucket
   415	 * might not cover a full bucket that we want to materialize:
   416	 *
   417	 * Refresh window:                   [-----)
   418	 * Materialized buckets:   |-----|-----|-----|
   419	 */
   420	static void
   421	validate_window_size(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, const CaggPolicyConfig *config)
   422	{
   423	        int64 start_offset;
   424	        int64 end_offset;
   425	        int64 bucket_width;
   426	
   427	        if (config->offset_start.isnull)
   428	                start_offset = ts_time_get_max(cagg->partition_type);
   429	        else
   430	                start_offset = interval_to_int64(config->offset_start.value, config->offset_start.type);
   431	
   432	        if (config->offset_end.isnull)
   433	                end_offset = ts_time_get_min(cagg->partition_type);
   434	        else
   435	                end_offset = interval_to_int64(config->offset_end.value, config->offset_end.type);
   436	
   437	        bucket_width = ts_continuous_agg_bucket_width(cagg->bucket_function);
   438	        Assert(bucket_width > 0);
   439	
   440	        if (ts_time_saturating_add(end_offset, bucket_width * 2, INT8OID) > start_offset)
   441	                ereport(ERROR,
   442	                                (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
   443	                                 errmsg("policy refresh window too small"),
   444	                                 errdetail("The start and end offsets must cover at least"
   445	                                                   " two buckets in the valid time range of type \"%s\".",
   446	                                                   format_type_be(cagg->partition_type))));
   447	}
   448	
   449	static void
   450	parse_offset_arg(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, Oid offset_type, NullableDatum arg,
   451	                                 ContinuousAggPolicyOffset *offset)
   452	{
   453	        offset->isnull = arg.isnull;
   454	
   455	        if (!offset->isnull)
   456	        {
   457	                offset->value =
   458	                        convert_interval_arg(cagg->partition_type, arg.value, &offset_type, offset->name);
   459	                offset->type = offset_type;
   460	        }
   461	}
   462	
   463	static void
   464	parse_cagg_policy_config(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, Oid start_offset_type,
   465	                                                 NullableDatum start_offset, Oid end_offset_type, NullableDatum end_offset,
   466	                                                 CaggPolicyConfig *config)
   467	{
   468	        MemSet(config, 0, sizeof(CaggPolicyConfig));
   469	        config->partition_type = cagg->partition_type;
   470	        /* This might seem backwards, but since we are dealing with offsets, start
   471	         * actually translates to max and end to min for maximum window. */
   472	        config->offset_start.value = ts_time_datum_get_max(config->partition_type);
   473	        config->offset_end.value = ts_time_datum_get_min(config->partition_type);
   474	        config->offset_start.type = config->offset_end.type =
   475	                IS_TIMESTAMP_TYPE(cagg->partition_type) ? INTERVALOID : cagg->partition_type;
   476	        config->offset_start.name = POL_REFRESH_CONF_KEY_START_OFFSET;
   477	        config->offset_end.name = POL_REFRESH_CONF_KEY_END_OFFSET;
   478	        parse_offset_arg(cagg, start_offset_type, start_offset, &config->offset_start);
   479	        parse_offset_arg(cagg, end_offset_type, end_offset, &config->offset_end);
   480	
   481	        Assert(config->offset_start.type == config->offset_end.type);
   482	        validate_window_size(cagg, config);
   483	}
   484	
   485	bool
   486	policy_refresh_cagg_check_if_last_policy(PolicyContinuousAggData *policy_data)
   487	{
   488	        ContinuousAgg *cagg = policy_data->cagg;
   489	        int64 end_offset = policy_data->refresh_window.end;
   490	        bool end_isnull = policy_data->refresh_window.end_isnull;
   491	
   492	        if (end_isnull)
   493	                return true;
   494	
   495	        Hypertable *mat_ht = ts_hypertable_get_by_id(cagg->data.mat_hypertable_id);
   496	        const Dimension *dim = get_open_dimension_for_hypertable(mat_ht, true);
   497	
   498	        List *jobs = ts_bgw_job_find_by_proc_and_hypertable_id(POLICY_REFRESH_CAGG_PROC_NAME,
   499	                                                                                                                   FUNCTIONS_SCHEMA_NAME,
   500	                                                                                                                   cagg->data.mat_hypertable_id);
   501	
   502	        ListCell *lc;
   503	
   504	        /* We need to go through all jobs in order to determine if there is a job which starts after
   505	         * this one */
   506	        foreach (lc, jobs)
   507	        {
   508	                BgwJob *job = (BgwJob *) lfirst(lc);
   509	
   510	                bool end_offset_job_isnull;
   511	                int64 end_offset_job =
   512	                        policy_refresh_cagg_get_refresh_end(dim, job->fd.config, &end_offset_job_isnull);
   513	
   514	                if (end_offset_job_isnull || end_offset < end_offset_job)
   515	                {
   516	                        return false;
   517	                }
   518	        }
   519	
   520	        return true;
   521	}
   522	
   523	/* Ensures the refresh range of the new policy doesn't overlap with an existing one*/
   524	PolicyRefreshOffsetOverlapResult
   525	policy_refresh_cagg_check_for_overlaps(ContinuousAgg *cagg, Jsonb *policy_config,
   526	                                                                           int32 existing_job_id)
   527	{
   528	        List *jobs = ts_bgw_job_find_by_proc_and_hypertable_id(POLICY_REFRESH_CAGG_PROC_NAME,
   529	                                                                                                                   FUNCTIONS_SCHEMA_NAME,
   530	                                                                                                                   cagg->data.mat_hypertable_id);
   531	        PolicyRefreshOffsetOverlapResult overlap_result = POLICY_REFRESH_OFFSET_OVERLAP_NONE;
   532	
   533	        if (jobs == NIL)
   534	                return overlap_result;

bool
policy_refresh_cagg_execute(int32 job_id, Jsonb *config)
{
	PolicyContinuousAggData policy_data;

	StringInfo str = makeStringInfo();
	JsonbToCStringIndent(str, &config->root, VARSIZE(config));

	policy_refresh_cagg_read_and_validate_config(config, &policy_data);
	bool extend_last_bucket = !policy_refresh_cagg_check_if_last_policy(&policy_data);

	bool enable_osm_reads_old = ts_guc_enable_osm_reads;

	if (!policy_data.include_tiered_data_isnull)
	{
		SetConfigOption("timescaledb.enable_tiered_reads",
						policy_data.include_tiered_data ? "on" : "off",
						PGC_USERSET,
						PGC_S_SESSION);
	}

	ContinuousAggRefreshContext context = { .callctx = CAGG_REFRESH_POLICY };

	/* Try to split window range into a list of ranges */
	List *refresh_window_list =
		continuous_agg_split_refresh_window(policy_data.cagg,
											&policy_data.refresh_window,
											policy_data.buckets_per_batch,
											policy_data.refresh_newest_first);
	if (refresh_window_list == NIL)
		refresh_window_list = lappend(refresh_window_list, &policy_data.refresh_window);
	else
		context.callctx = CAGG_REFRESH_POLICY_BATCHED;

	context.number_of_batches = list_length(refresh_window_list);

	ListCell *lc;
	int32 processing_batch = 0;
	foreach (lc, refresh_window_list)
	{
		InternalTimeRange *refresh_window = (InternalTimeRange *) lfirst(lc);
		elog(DEBUG1,
			 "refreshing continuous aggregate \"%s\" from %s to %s",
			 NameStr(policy_data.cagg->data.user_view_name),
			 ts_internal_to_time_string(refresh_window->start, refresh_window->type),
			 ts_internal_to_time_string(refresh_window->end, refresh_window->type));

		context.processing_batch = ++processing_batch;
		continuous_agg_refresh_internal(policy_data.cagg,
										refresh_window,
										context,
										refresh_window->start_isnull,

   731	continuous_agg_refresh_internal(const ContinuousAgg *cagg,

   733	                                                                const ContinuousAggRefreshContext context, const bool start_isnull,
   734	                                                                const bool end_isnull, bool bucketing_refresh_window, bool force,
   735	                                                                bool process_hypertable_invalidations, bool extend_last_bucket)
   736	{
   737	        int32 mat_id = cagg->data.mat_hypertable_id;
   738	        InternalTimeRange refresh_window = *refresh_window_arg;
   739	        int64 invalidation_threshold;
   740	        bool nonatomic = ts_process_utility_is_context_nonatomic();
   741	
   742	        /* Reset the saved ProcessUtilityContext value promptly before
   743	         * calling Prevent* checks so the potential unsupported (atomic)
   744	         * value won't linger there in case of ereport exit.
   745	         */
   746	        ts_process_utility_context_reset();
   747	
   748	        PreventCommandIfReadOnly(REFRESH_FUNCTION_NAME);
   749	
   750	        /* Prevent running refresh if we're in a transaction block since a refresh
   751	         * can run two transactions and might take a long time to release locks if
   752	         * there's a lot to materialize. Strictly, it is optional to prohibit
   753	         * transaction blocks since there will be only one transaction if the
   754	         * invalidation threshold needs no update. However, materialization might
   755	         * still take a long time and it is probably best for consistency to always
   756	         * prevent transaction blocks.  */
   757	        PreventInTransactionBlock(nonatomic, REFRESH_FUNCTION_NAME);
   758	
   759	        /*
   760	         * We don't cagg refresh to fail because of decompression limit. So disable
   761	         * the decompression limit for the duration of the refresh.
   762	         */
   763	        const char *old_decompression_limit =
   764	                GetConfigOption("timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction", false, false);
   765	        SetConfigOption("timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction",
   766	                                        "0",
   767	                                        PGC_USERSET,
   768	                                        PGC_S_SESSION);
   769	
   770	        /* Connect to SPI manager due to the underlying SPI calls */
   771	        int rc = SPI_connect_ext(SPI_OPT_NONATOMIC);
   772	        if (rc != SPI_OK_CONNECT)
   773	                elog(ERROR, "SPI_connect failed: %s", SPI_result_code_string(rc));
   774	
   775	        /* Lock down search_path */
   776	        int save_nestlevel = NewGUCNestLevel();
   777	        RestrictSearchPath();

   779	        /* Like regular materialized views, require owner to refresh. */
   780	        if (!object_ownercheck(RelationRelationId, cagg->relid, GetUserId()))
   781	                aclcheck_error(ACLCHECK_NOT_OWNER,
   782	                                           get_relkind_objtype(get_rel_relkind(cagg->relid)),
   783	                                           get_rel_name(cagg->relid));
   784	
   785	        /* No bucketing when open ended */
   786	        if (bucketing_refresh_window && !(start_isnull && end_isnull))
   787	        {
   788	                if (cagg->bucket_function->bucket_fixed_interval == false)
   789	                {
   790	                        refresh_window = *refresh_window_arg;
   791	                        ts_compute_inscribed_bucketed_refresh_window_variable(&refresh_window.start,
   792	                                                                                                                                  &refresh_window.end,
   793	                                                                                                                                  cagg->bucket_function);
   794	                }
   795	                else
   796	                {
   797	                        int64 bucket_width = ts_continuous_agg_fixed_bucket_width(cagg->bucket_function);
   798	                        Assert(bucket_width > 0);
   799	                        refresh_window =
   800	                                compute_inscribed_bucketed_refresh_window(cagg, refresh_window_arg, bucket_width);
   801	                }
   802	        }
   803	
   804	        if (refresh_window.start >= refresh_window.end)
   805	                ereport(ERROR,
   806	                                (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
   807	                                 errmsg("refresh window too small"),
   808	                                 errdetail("The refresh window must cover at least one bucket of data."),
   809	                                 errhint("Align the refresh window with the bucket"
   810	                                                 " time zone or use at least two buckets.")));
   811	
   812	        /* If there is no other policy defined after this, the inscribed bucket calculated above
   813	         * is correct. However, in the case of concurrent policies, if this isn't the last
   814	         * policy defined then we should extend the end of the window to include the partial
   815	         * bucket. This is done to ensure concurrent policies that are 'adjacent' don't skip a
   816	         * bucket We don't need to do this when the CAgg is created WITH DATA, or manually
   817	         * refreshed
   818	         */
   819	        if (extend_last_bucket && !(start_isnull && end_isnull))
   820	        {
   821	                if (cagg->bucket_function->bucket_fixed_interval == false)
   822	                {
   823	                        refresh_window.end =
   824	                                ts_compute_beginning_of_the_next_bucket_variable(refresh_window.end,
   825	                                                                                                                                 cagg->bucket_function);
   826	                }
   827	                else
   828	                {
   829	                        int64 bucket_width = ts_continuous_agg_fixed_bucket_width(cagg->bucket_function);
   830	                        refresh_window.end =
   831	                                ts_time_saturating_add(refresh_window.end, bucket_width - 1, refresh_window.type);
   832	                }
   833	        }
   834	
   835	        /*
   836	         * Perform the refresh across two transactions.
   837	         *
   838	         * The first transaction moves the invalidation threshold (if needed) and
   839	         * copies over invalidations from the hypertable log to the cagg
   840	         * invalidation log. Doing the threshold and copying as part of the first
   841	         * transaction ensures that the threshold and new invalidations will be
   842	         * visible as soon as possible to concurrent refreshes and that we keep
   843	         * locks for only a short period.
   844	         *
   845	         * The second transaction processes the cagg invalidation log and then
   846	         * performs the actual refresh (materialization of data). This transaction
   847	         * serializes around a lock on the materialized hypertable for the
   848	         * continuous aggregate that gets refreshed.
   849	         */
   850

str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_timezone_issue.sql --file_text '-- Test script to reproduce the timezone issue with continuous aggregates

-- Create test environment
CREATE TABLE metrics (
    sensor_id INTEGER NOT NULL,
    value DOUBLE PRECISION NOT NULL,
    timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL
);

SELECT create_hypertable('"'"'metrics'"'"', '"'"'timestamp'"'"');

-- Insert some test data
INSERT INTO metrics
SELECT
    s.sensor_id,
    random()*50 + 10,
    timestamp
FROM
    generate_series(DATE (now() - interval '"'"'6 month'"'"'), (now() - interval '"'"'5 day'"'"'), INTERVAL '"'"'1 hours'"'"') AS timestamp
        CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 200) as sensor_id) as s;

-- Create continuous aggregate with timezone
CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW datalake_hourly
WITH (timescaledb.continuous, timescaledb.materialized_only = true) AS
            SELECT
                time_bucket(INTERVAL '"'"'1 hour'"'"', metrics.timestamp, '"'"'Asia/Dubai'"'"') AS bucket,
                sensor_id,
                count(*) as count_items
            FROM metrics
            GROUP BY bucket, sensor_id;

-- Add continuous aggregate policy
SELECT add_continuous_aggregate_policy(
        '"'"'datalake_hourly'"'"',
        start_offset => INTERVAL '"'"'3 months'"'"',
        end_offset => NULL,
        schedule_interval => INTERVAL '"'"'15 seconds'"'"'
);

-- Insert more recent data
INSERT INTO metrics
SELECT
    s.sensor_id,
    random()*50 + 10,
    timestamp
FROM
    generate_series((now() - interval '"'"'5 day'"'"'), now(), INTERVAL '"'"'1 hour'"'"') AS timestamp
        CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 200) as sensor_id) as s;

-- Wait a bit for the policy to run
DO LANGUAGE plpgsql $$
BEGIN
    PERFORM pg_sleep(30);
END;
$$;

-- Check job status
SELECT 
    job_id,
    application_name,
    last_run_status,
    total_failures,
    total_successes
FROM timescaledb_information.job_stats 
WHERE job_id IN (
    SELECT job_id 
    FROM timescaledb_information.jobs 
    WHERE hypertable_name LIKE '"'"'%datalake_hourly%'"'"'
);

-- Check data in continuous aggregate
SELECT count(*) FROM datalake_hourly;
SELECT max(bucket) FROM datalake_hourly;
SELECT max(timestamp) FROM metrics;'

Based on my analysis of the codebase, I've identified the root cause of the issue with continuous aggregates using `time_bucket` with timezones. The problem lies in the `TIME_BUCKET_TS` macro in `/testbed/src/time_bucket.c`.

## Root Cause Analysis

The "timestamp out of range" error occurs when:
1. Continuous aggregates use `time_bucket` with timezone parameters (e.g., `time_bucket('1 hour', timestamp, 'Asia/Dubai')`)
2. During refresh operations, the timezone conversion can result in timestamp values that are near the boundaries of valid timestamp ranges
3. The `TIME_BUCKET_TS` macro's range checking logic doesn't properly handle these edge cases when timezone conversions are involved

## The Fix

I've modified the `TIME_BUCKET_TS` macro to add a check for infinite timestamps before performing the range check. This prevents the "timestamp out of range" error when dealing with timezone conversions that might result in boundary values.

The change adds this check:
```c
/* Check if timestamp is finite before doing range check to avoid overflow */
if (TIMESTAMP_NOT_FINITE(timestamp))
{
    (result) = (timestamp);
    break;
}
```

This ensures that infinite timestamps (which can occur during timezone conversions) are handled properly and don't trigger the range check error.

## Why This Fix Works

1. **Timezone Conversions**: When timestamps are converted between timezones, values near the boundaries of valid timestamps can become infinite (`-infinity` or `+infinity`)

2. **Range Check Issue**: The original code would attempt to perform arithmetic operations on these infinite values, leading to overflow and the "out of range" error

3. **Early Exit**: By checking for infinite timestamps early and returning them as-is, we avoid the problematic range check and arithmetic operations

## Testing the Fix

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+"""
+Script to reproduce the continuous aggregate timezone issue.
+This script creates a PostgreSQL database and attempts to reproduce the bug.
+"""
+
+import subprocess
+import time
+import psycopg2
+import sys
+
+# PostgreSQL connection parameters
+DB_HOST = "localhost"
+DB_PORT = "5432"
+DB_NAME = "test_db"
+DB_USER = "postgres"
+DB_PASSWORD = "password"
+
+def run_sql(sql):
+    """Execute SQL command and return result"""
+    try:
+        conn = psycopg2.connect(
+            host=DB_HOST,
+            port=DB_PORT,
+            database=DB_NAME,
+            user=DB_USER,
+            password=DB_PASSWORD
+        )
+        conn.autocommit = True
+        cursor = conn.cursor()
+        cursor.execute(sql)
+        
+        if cursor.description:
+            result = cursor.fetchall()
+        else:
+            result = None
+            
+        conn.close()
+        return result
+    except Exception as e:
+        print(f"Error executing SQL: {e}")
+        return None
+
+def create_test_environment():
+    """Create the test environment as described in the PR"""
+    print("Creating test environment...")
+    
+    # Create the hypertable
+    run_sql("""
+    CREATE TABLE metrics (
+        sensor_id INTEGER NOT NULL,
+        value DOUBLE PRECISION NOT NULL,
+        timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL
+    );
+    """)
+    
+    run_sql("SELECT create_hypertable('metrics', 'timestamp');")
+    
+    # Insert data
+    run_sql("""
+    INSERT INTO metrics
+    SELECT
+        s.sensor_id,
+        random()*50 + 10,
+        timestamp
+    FROM
+        generate_series(DATE (now() - interval '6 month'), (now() - interval '5 day'), INTERVAL '1 hours') AS timestamp
+            CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 200) as sensor_id) as s;
+    """)
+    
+    # Create continuous aggregate with timezone
+    run_sql("""
+    CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW datalake_hourly
+    WITH (timescaledb.continuous, timescaledb.materialized_only = true) AS
+                SELECT
+                    time_bucket(INTERVAL '1 hour', metrics.timestamp, 'Asia/Dubai') AS bucket,
+                    sensor_id,
+                    count(*) as count_items
+                FROM metrics
+                GROUP BY bucket, sensor_id;
+    """)
+    
+    # Add continuous aggregate policy
+    run_sql("""
+    SELECT add_continuous_aggregate_policy(
+            'datalake_hourly',
+            start_offset => INTERVAL '3 months',
+            end_offset => Null,
+            schedule_interval => INTERVAL '15 seconds'
+    );
+    """)
+    
+    # Insert more data
+    run_sql("""
+    INSERT INTO metrics
+    SELECT
+        s.sensor_id,
+        random()*50 + 10,
+        timestamp
+    FROM
+        generate_series((now() - interval '5 day'), now(), INTERVAL '1 hour') AS timestamp
+            CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 200) as sensor_id) as s;
+    """)
+
+def check_job_status():
+    """Check the status of the continuous aggregate job"""
+    print("\nChecking job status...")
+    
+    result = run_sql("""
+    SELECT 
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.job_id,
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.application_name,
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.initial_start,
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.next_start,
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.config,
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.schedule_interval,
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.max_runtime ,
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.max_retries  ,   
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.retry_period ,  
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.scheduled ,
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.fixed_schedule , 
+            timescaledb_information.jobs.hypertable_name , 
+            timescaledb_information.continuous_aggregates.view_name ,
+            last_run_started_at ,
+           job_status,
+           last_run_status,
+           last_successful_finish ,
+           total_runs,
+           total_failures ,
+           total_successes 
+    FROM timescaledb_information.jobs
+    left join timescaledb_information.job_stats on timescaledb_information.jobs.job_id  =  timescaledb_information.job_stats.job_id 
+    left join timescaledb_information.continuous_aggregates on timescaledb_information.continuous_aggregates.materialization_hypertable_name  =  timescaledb_information.jobs.hypertable_name

+    result = run_sql("SELECT count(*) FROM datalake_hourly;")
+    if result:

+    """)

+    SELECT max(timestamp) FROM metrics;
+    """)

+        Datum timestamp = PG_GETARG_DATUM(1);
+        Datum tzname = PG_GETARG_DATUM(2);
+
+        /*
+         * When called from SQL we will always have 5 args because default values
+         * will be filled in for missing arguments. When called from C with
+         * DirectFunctionCall number of arguments might be less than 5.
+         */
+        bool have_origin = PG_NARGS() > 3 && !PG_ARGISNULL(3);
+        bool have_offset = PG_NARGS() > 4 && !PG_ARGISNULL(4);
+
+        /*
+         * We need to check for NULL arguments here because the function cannot be
+         * defined STRICT due to the optional arguments.
+         */
+        if (PG_ARGISNULL(0) || PG_ARGISNULL(1) || PG_ARGISNULL(2))
+                PG_RETURN_NULL();
+
+        /* Convert to local timestamp according to timezone */
+        timestamp = DirectFunctionCall2(timestamptz_zone, tzname, timestamp);
+        if (have_offset)
+        {
+                /* Apply offset. */
+                timestamp = DirectFunctionCall2(timestamp_mi_interval, timestamp, PG_GETARG_DATUM(4));
+        }
+
+        if (have_origin)
+        {
+                Datum origin = DirectFunctionCall2(timestamptz_zone, tzname, PG_GETARG_DATUM(3));
+                timestamp = DirectFunctionCall3(ts_timestamp_bucket, period, timestamp, origin);
+        }
+        else
+        {
+                timestamp = DirectFunctionCall2(ts_timestamp_bucket, period, timestamp);
+        }
+
+        if (have_offset)
+        {
+                /* Remove offset. */
+                timestamp = DirectFunctionCall2(timestamp_pl_interval, timestamp, PG_GETARG_DATUM(4));
+        }
+
+        /* Convert back to timezone */
+        timestamp = DirectFunctionCall2(timestamp_zone, tzname, timestamp);
+
+        PG_RETURN_DATUM(timestamp);
 }

+                ereport(ERROR,
+                                (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
+                                 errmsg("origin must be the first day of the month"),
+                                 errhint("When using timestamptz-version of the function, 'origin' is "
+                                                 "converted to provided 'timezone'.")));
+        }
+
+        if (DATE_NOT_FINITE(date))
+                PG_RETURN_DATEADT(date);
+
+        if (interval->month != 0)
+        {
+                /* Handle months and years */
+
+                j2date(date + POSTGRES_EPOCH_JDATE, &year, &month, &day);
+                int32 result;
+                int32 offset = (origin_year * 12) + origin_month - 1;
+                int32 timestamp = (year * 12) + month - 1;
+                TIME_BUCKET(interval->month, timestamp, offset, PG_INT32_MIN, PG_INT32_MAX, result);
+
+                year = result / 12;
+                month = (result % 12) + 1;
+                day = 1;
+
+                date = date2j(year, month, day) - POSTGRES_EPOCH_JDATE;
+        }
+        else
+        {
+                /* Handle days and weeks */
+
+                if (date < origin_date)
+                {
+                        ereport(ERROR,
+                                        (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
+                                         errmsg("origin must be before the given date")));
+                }
+
+                delta = date - origin_date;
+                bucket_number = delta / interval->day;
+                date = origin_date + bucket_number * interval->day;
+        }
+
+        PG_RETURN_DATEADT(date);
 }

+-- Test script to reproduce the timezone issue with continuous aggregates
+
+-- Create test environment
+CREATE TABLE metrics (
+    sensor_id INTEGER NOT NULL,
+    value DOUBLE PRECISION NOT NULL,
+    timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL
+);
+
+SELECT create_hypertable('metrics', 'timestamp');
+
+-- Insert some test data
+INSERT INTO metrics
+SELECT
+    s.sensor_id,
+    random()*50 + 10,
+    timestamp
+FROM
+    generate_series(DATE (now() - interval '6 month'), (now() - interval '5 day'), INTERVAL '1 hours') AS timestamp
+        CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 200) as sensor_id) as s;
+
+-- Create continuous aggregate with timezone
+CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW datalake_hourly
+WITH (timescaledb.continuous, timescaledb.materialized_only = true) AS
+            SELECT
+                time_bucket(INTERVAL '1 hour', metrics.timestamp, 'Asia/Dubai') AS bucket,
+                sensor_id,
+                count(*) as count_items
+            FROM metrics
+            GROUP BY bucket, sensor_id;
+
+-- Add continuous aggregate policy
+SELECT add_continuous_aggregate_policy(
+        'datalake_hourly',
+        start_offset => INTERVAL '3 months',
+        end_offset => NULL,
+        schedule_interval => INTERVAL '15 seconds'
+);
+
+-- Insert more recent data
+INSERT INTO metrics
+SELECT
+    s.sensor_id,
+    random()*50 + 10,
+    timestamp
+FROM
+    generate_series((now() - interval '5 day'), now(), INTERVAL '1 hour') AS timestamp
+        CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 200) as sensor_id) as s;
+
+-- Wait a bit for the policy to run
+DO LANGUAGE plpgsql $$
+BEGIN
+    PERFORM pg_sleep(30);
+END;
+$$;
+
+-- Check job status
+SELECT 
+    job_id,
+    application_name,
+    last_run_status,
+    total_failures,
+    total_successes
+FROM timescaledb_information.job_stats 
+WHERE job_id IN (
+    SELECT job_id 
+    FROM timescaledb_information.jobs 
+    WHERE hypertable_name LIKE '%datalake_hourly%'
+);
+
+-- Check data in continuous aggregate
+SELECT count(*) FROM datalake_hourly;
+SELECT max(bucket) FROM datalake_hourly;
+SELECT max(timestamp) FROM metrics;
\ No newline at end of file

</diff>

+

+                month = (result % 12) + 1;
+                day = 1;
+
+                date = date2j(year, month, day) - POSTGRES_EPOCH_JDATE;
+        }
+        else
+        {
+                /* Handle days and weeks */
+
+                if (date < origin_date)
+                {
+                        ereport(ERROR,
+                                        (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
+                                         errmsg("origin must be before the given date")));
+                }
+
+                delta = date - origin_date;
+                bucket_number = delta / interval->day;
+                date = origin_date + bucket_number * interval->day;
+        }
+
+        PG_RETURN_DATEADT(date);

+        /* Defined offset and origin in one function is not supported */
+        Assert(offset.isnull == true || origin.isnull == true);
+
+        Datum timestamp_in_time_type = ts_internal_to_time_value(timestamp, timestamp_type);
+        Datum interval_in_interval_type;
+        Datum time_bucketed;
+        Datum (*bucket_function)(PG_FUNCTION_ARGS);
+
+        switch (timestamp_type)
+        {
+                case INT2OID:
+                        interval_in_interval_type = ts_internal_to_interval_value(interval, timestamp_type);
+                        bucket_function = ts_int16_bucket;
+                        break;
+                case INT4OID:
+                        interval_in_interval_type = ts_internal_to_interval_value(interval, timestamp_type);
+                        bucket_function = ts_int32_bucket;
+                        break;
+                case INT8OID:
+                        interval_in_interval_type = ts_internal_to_interval_value(interval, timestamp_type);
+                        bucket_function = ts_int64_bucket;
+                        break;
+                case TIMESTAMPOID:
+                        interval_in_interval_type = ts_internal_to_interval_value(interval, INTERVALOID);
+                        if (offset.isnull)
+                                bucket_function = ts_timestamp_bucket; /* handles also origin */
+                        else
+                                bucket_function = ts_timestamp_offset_bucket;
+                        break;
+                case TIMESTAMPTZOID:
+                        interval_in_interval_type = ts_internal_to_interval_value(interval, INTERVALOID);
+                        if (offset.isnull)
+                                bucket_function = ts_timestamptz_bucket; /* handles also origin */
+                        else
+                                bucket_function = ts_timestamptz_offset_bucket;
+                        break;
+                case DATEOID:
+                        interval_in_interval_type = ts_internal_to_interval_value(interval, INTERVALOID);
+                        if (offset.isnull)
+                                bucket_function = ts_date_bucket; /* handles also origin */
+                        else
+                                bucket_function = ts_date_offset_bucket;
+                        break;
+                default:
+                        elog(ERROR, "invalid time_bucket type \"%s\"", format_type_be(timestamp_type));
+        }
+
+        if (!offset.isnull)
+        {
+                time_bucketed = DirectFunctionCall3(bucket_function,
+                                                                                        interval_in_interval_type,
+                                                                                        timestamp_in_time_type,
+                                                                                        offset.value);
+        }
+        else if (!origin.isnull)
+        {
+                time_bucketed = DirectFunctionCall3(bucket_function,
+                                                                                        interval_in_interval_type,
+                                                                                        timestamp_in_time_type,
+                                                                                        origin.value);
+        }
+        else
+        {
+                time_bucketed =
+                        DirectFunctionCall2(bucket_function, interval_in_interval_type, timestamp_in_time_type);
+        }
+
+        return ts_time_value_to_internal(time_bucketed, timestamp_type);
 }

+                if (DATE_NOT_FINITE(origin_date))

+

+        {
+                ereport(ERROR,
+                                (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
+                                 errmsg("origin must be the first day of the month"),
+                                 errhint("When using timestamptz-version of the function, 'origin' is "

+        }
+

+                PG_RETURN_DATEADT(date);
+

+        {
+                /* Handle months and years */
+
+                j2date(date + POSTGRES_EPOCH_JDATE, &year, &month, &day);
+                int32 result;
+                int32 offset = (origin_year * 12) + origin_month - 1;
+                int32 timestamp = (year * 12) + month - 1;
+                TIME_BUCKET(interval->month, timestamp, offset, PG_INT32_MIN, PG_INT32_MAX, result);
+
+                year = result / 12;
+                month = (result % 12) + 1;
+                day = 1;
+
+                date = date2j(year, month, day) - POSTGRES_EPOCH_JDATE;
+        }
+        else
+        {
+                /* Handle days and weeks */
+
+                if (date < origin_date)
+                {
+                        ereport(ERROR,
+                                        (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
+                                         errmsg("origin must be before the given date")));
+                }
+
+                delta = date - origin_date;
+                bucket_number = delta / interval->day;
+                date = origin_date + bucket_number * interval->day;
+        }
+
+        PG_RETURN_DATEADT(date);
 }
